<div id="review_280845264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280845264" />
    <a title="Ellen " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6504086-ellen"><img alt="Ellen " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1359564377p2/6504086.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280845264?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellen " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellen " href="/user/show/6504086-ellen">Ellen </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280845264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15803359808036513662">I have been anxiously awaiting this book since I read Existence, the first in the series. I love Abbi Glines and she has written another great paranormal romance in the second book of the Existence Trilogy, which is also filled with suspense, intrigue, and delves deep into the paranormal.<br/><br/>We came to know and love Dank (AKA Death) and Pagan in Existence. Pagan was a normal high school student who could see dead souls, which she ignored, and for the most part they left her alone when she ignored th</span>
  <span id="freeText15803359808036513662" style="display:none">I have been anxiously awaiting this book since I read Existence, the first in the series. I love Abbi Glines and she has written another great paranormal romance in the second book of the Existence Trilogy, which is also filled with suspense, intrigue, and delves deep into the paranormal.<br /><br />We came to know and love Dank (AKA Death) and Pagan in Existence. Pagan was a normal high school student who could see dead souls, which she ignored, and for the most part they left her alone when she ignored them. Then she meets Dank Walker, and he not only talks to her, he is smoking hot. Dank just thought he was coming to take another soul, he didn't expect to fall in love with Pagan and end up breaking all the rules. Predestined picks up where Existence left off. Pagan's selfless choice at the end of Existence (and if you haven't read it you will need to in order to find out what that was), has allowed she and Dank to be together. Just when she thought things were getting better, they find out that her old boyfriend, Lief, isn't what he seemed at all. He's not human, he doesn't even have a soul, and he has a claim on Pagan's soul that she and Dank never even imagined. He invades her dreams and is determined that he is going to have Pagan, sucking her into his evil realm. Dank, of course, is not about to let that happen and vows that nobody and I mean nobody, is going to have Pagan but him, as they are thrust into a world of darkness and voodoo, shrouded in evil, in order to redeem Pagan's soul. The situations that Pagan, her friends, and family have go through are heart wrenching and Pagan is determined to do whatever she needs to in order to keep her friends and family safe, while Dank is going to do whatever he needs to in order to keep Pagan safe. Despite all the heartache, there are also moments of pure joy and the romance between Pagan and Dank is really hot, and to top it off he is a rock star also.<br /><br />I really loved this story. Only Abbi Glines could make Death such a hottie and so swoon worthy. The paranormal world Abbi has created in the Existence Trilogy is intriguing and exciting, and kind of scary at times. I loved Gee, whose character brings so much humor into some serious situations. Predestined gives you view points from both Pagan and Dank's point of view, and it was really great getting to know Dank more in this book, being able to get inside his head and understanding what a great guy he really is. The suspense is intense and keeps you turning the pages to see what happens next, and the ending totally has me ever so anxiously awaiting the third book in the series, Ceaseless. This is an awesome book, but then again, Abbi Glines never disappoints. Enjoy it, oh yes I did. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15803359808036513662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5608085091764527762"><b>4 Twist & Turn Stars</b><br/><br/>Wow. Abbi did it again. Sometimes I forget that Abbi even wrote this series. It's fantastic. And yes, once AGAIN, she played havoc with my tear ducts and heart strings. <br/><br/><b> What I loved:</b><br/>1. The unexpected twists and turns<br/>2. My love/hate relationship with Leif<br/>3.   <span id="freeText5608085091764527762" style="display:none"><b>4 Twist &amp; Turn Stars</b><br /><br />Wow. Abbi did it again. Sometimes I forget that Abbi even wrote this series. It's fantastic. And yes, once AGAIN, she played havoc with my tear ducts and heart strings. <br /><br /><b> What I loved:</b><br />1. The unexpected twists and turns<br />2. My love/hate relationship with Leif<br />3. Dual POV's of Dank &amp; Pagan<br />4. Gee. How can you NOT love this crazy lady!<br />5. Being able to be with Death on his jobs in different kinds of scenarios<br />6. LOVED how this one ended as it left a bit of suspense<br /><br />I'm excited to see a certain "soul" among the living and how that will all play out. <br /><br />Once again Abbi was able to hold my attention with her writing. Never once did I want to cheat and read the ending first then go back and read it from the beginning. I was captivated and barely could put the book down. I will admit it: I. Am. A. Book. Crier. So yes, I CRIED a bit in this. Abbi sure knows how to write certain heart wrenching scenes in book 1 and 2. I loved the story line. Although, there were times I felt like Death wasn't necessarily doing a good job at keeping his SOUL/Girl safe. I felt like Leif gave up to easily in a certain part. I also felt like the big "OH-NO" scene ended a bit too easily as well and Ghede sure gave up a certain soul easily too. I also wanted Death to be a little more scarier. ;o) But, hey...it all worked out in the end and maybe for once a big drawn out scene with angst, drama and bad villain's didn't need to be. Whatever the case may be, I still loved this story and it's keeping me out of the book funk and right in the happy book coma I want to be in. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7099775562353358255">This book was good but not great. Honestly it seemed a little unfocused and disjointed to me. I guess I got that the central theme was about fending Leif off from Pagan's dreams, but for some reason the plot just didn't seem as strong to me as the first one did. That and the climax of this book seemed a little anticlimatic. Or I guess just everything in this book was like that for me, good but not great, I liked it but I didn't really feel a part of the book and I wasn't engrossed in it and lost</span>
  <span id="freeText7099775562353358255" style="display:none">This book was good but not great. Honestly it seemed a little unfocused and disjointed to me. I guess I got that the central theme was about fending Leif off from Pagan's dreams, but for some reason the plot just didn't seem as strong to me as the first one did. That and the climax of this book seemed a little anticlimatic. Or I guess just everything in this book was like that for me, good but not great, I liked it but I didn't really feel a part of the book and I wasn't engrossed in it and lost in their world. It was like I was still an outsider looking in and I guess that's why overall I just didn't end up feeling very attached to this book.<br /><br />Nonetheless I'm still very excited for the next and final installment of this series! As always, Abbi Glines' summarys are such suckers and she's set this up perfectly for the next book. On that note, I really like the sequence of the plots in her books. They fit really well with one another and make sense.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SwJK+TGbL2PxHoDN2USUiT0dFDLATDIwBIN1nbREyggcZfxvsNuwl39KH9YxxIlPM8HxWuqPs2cU/OPOrtDhiQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kc6KFuBQIx0aDxiGO2Sava4CWI3vJMMC57jFmVU7vxjGqTyAYRC86ZRbh53T5Id7oN695cXnQlX3x1PKT6+UmQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer15681082334677913021">Abbi Glines is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of the Rosemary Beach, Sea Breeze, Vincent Boys, Field Party and Existence series. She never cooks unless baking during the Christmas holiday counts. She believes in ghosts and has a habit of asking people if their house is haunted before she goes in it. She drinks afternoon tea because she wants to be Britis</span>
  <span id="freeText15681082334677913021" style="display:none">Abbi Glines is a #1 New York Times, USA Today, and Wall Street Journal bestselling author of the Rosemary Beach, Sea Breeze, Vincent Boys, Field Party and Existence series. She never cooks unless baking during the Christmas holiday counts. She believes in ghosts and has a habit of asking people if their house is haunted before she goes in it. She drinks afternoon tea because she wants to be British but alas she was born in Alabama. When asked how many books she has written she has to stop and count on her fingers. When she’s not locked away writing, she is reading, shopping (major shoe and purse addiction), sneaking off to the movies alone, and listening to the drama in her teenagers lives while making mental notes on the good stuff to use later. Don’t judge.<br /><br />You can connect with Abbi online in several different ways. She uses social media to procrastinate.<br /></span>
